  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_40a48458-72d9-4e4f-b25b-b42eee397d0e'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer16886865467541862639">Aeriel's love has broken the curse on the darkangel Irrylath, making him human again and freeing him from the control of his mother, the dreaded White Witch.   <span id="freeText16886865467541862639" style="display:none">Aeriel's love has broken the curse on the darkangel Irrylath, making him human again and freeing him from the control of his mother, the dreaded White Witch. But the Witch is far from defeated. Her wicked plans require all seven of her vampyre sons, and she will not give one up so easily. There is but a single hope for the Witch's defeat--solving an ancient, mysterious riddle. So Aeriel sets off to solve the riddle, sailing across a sea of dust and straight into the worst of the Witch's terrors. But if Aeriel is to save Irrylath and her world, she will have to overcome his bloodthirsty darkangel brothers--and ultimately confront his terrifying mother face-to-face.<br /></span>

<div id="review_517692516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/517692516" />
    <a title="Lauren Schumacher" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13898750-lauren-schumacher"><img alt="Lauren Schumacher" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351023423p2/13898750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/517692516?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren Schumacher" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren Schumacher" href="/user/show/13898750-lauren-schumacher">Lauren Schumacher</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780812549027" href="/book/show/1189719.A_Gathering_of_Gargoyles">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer517692516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1798915537843754333">The first book is a trial, and the second book is a journey. What always strikes me about this installment is our heroine's transformation into...a prophet, a sorceress, a scientist, take your pick. All her seemingly magical feats are explained so easily to her (and to us) as "help from another" or "not my doing" or "not what I intended." It reminds me of becoming an adult woman--a string of events mostly outside of your control makes you become sought-after, hated, desirable, a prize to control</span>
  <span id="freeText1798915537843754333" style="display:none">The first book is a trial, and the second book is a journey. What always strikes me about this installment is our heroine's transformation into...a prophet, a sorceress, a scientist, take your pick. All her seemingly magical feats are explained so easily to her (and to us) as "help from another" or "not my doing" or "not what I intended." It reminds me of becoming an adult woman--a string of events mostly outside of your control makes you become sought-after, hated, desirable, a prize to control. Aeriel's journey proves that she is still very much a child--a child still in love with her first, most inappropriate crush. The ending of this book always entranced and terrified me. The "Sibyl," the Feasting Stone, the slave markets of Orm...Aeriel's consistent fear of being re=enslaved, of becoming ignorant and passive again, is most telling of her development. She can't articulate that she's free, but she instinctively defends it.<br /><br />I used to feel such smug joy to find that Irrylath traveled halfway around the world to apologize for, essentially, not loving her back. But as an adult I can see that his journey mirrors hers, just tragically out of sync. When they meet again, it is still as two strangers who would chase the idea of each other to hell and back but still, painfully, have nothing to say to each other.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1798915537843754333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1330468366" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3919132-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507125560p2/3919132.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1330468366?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/3919132-linda">Linda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316067256" href="/book/show/1877307.A_Gathering_of_Gargoyles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=strong-female">strong-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=magic-involved">magic-involved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=young-adult-story">young-adult-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=fantasy-adventure">fantasy-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3919132-linda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1330468366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2231917002956828931">Following on the heels of THE DARKANGEL, Aeriel and Irrylath were married but in name only. She was aware something was amiss and, before long, took it upon herself to find out why. A riddle, her staff, the gargoyles and magic accompanied her on another adventure.<br/><br/>I fell in love with the author's unusual words, crisp descriptions (especially of food) and the many gray areas of the plot. Each character Aeriel met taught her something about her destiny without her actually aware of it. By the time </span>
  <span id="freeText2231917002956828931" style="display:none">Following on the heels of THE DARKANGEL, Aeriel and Irrylath were married but in name only. She was aware something was amiss and, before long, took it upon herself to find out why. A riddle, her staff, the gargoyles and magic accompanied her on another adventure.<br /><br />I fell in love with the author's unusual words, crisp descriptions (especially of food) and the many gray areas of the plot. Each character Aeriel met taught her something about her destiny without her actually aware of it. By the time I finished this story I realized I had to read THE PEARL OF THE SOUL OF THE WORLD as soon as possible. <br /><br />I wanted closure for <i>Aeriel and all of her fellow travellers</i>. I sought a finality to the White Witch. And, most importantly, I desired a happy denouement for Aeriel and Irrylath.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2231917002956828931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_26194712" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26194712" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1215148-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26194712?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/1215148-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316067256" href="/book/show/1877307.A_Gathering_of_Gargoyles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1215148-emily?shelf=ya-childrens_lit">ya-childrens_lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1215148-emily?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1215148-emily?shelf=2008-07">2008-07</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26194712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18107949039315885503">This review is for <i>A Gathering of Gargoyles</i> and <i>The Pearl of the Soul of the World</i>…<br/><br/>Some might think that the <i>Darkangel Trilogy</i> is in the paranormal genre because of the vampires, but it isn’t. It is mostly fantasy and even a little sci-fi. Pierce creates worlds, new species, and terminology. <br/><br/>The cover quote describes the books as Heart-warming and Heart-breaking and it truly is. Aeriel is a good heroine who follows the path of self discovery. She learns that to do great things it requires sacrif</span>
  <span id="freeText18107949039315885503" style="display:none">This review is for <i>A Gathering of Gargoyles</i> and <i>The Pearl of the Soul of the World</i>…<br /><br />Some might think that the <i>Darkangel Trilogy</i> is in the paranormal genre because of the vampires, but it isn’t. It is mostly fantasy and even a little sci-fi. Pierce creates worlds, new species, and terminology. <br /><br />The cover quote describes the books as Heart-warming and Heart-breaking and it truly is. Aeriel is a good heroine who follows the path of self discovery. She learns that to do great things it requires sacrifice. Nothing comes easy. Anything worth having is worth working for. I love that message. <br /><br />The other main characters Prince Irrylath and Erin are very relatable. At first, Prince Irrylath seems uncaring and indifferent towards Aeriel. Aeriel even calls him her “husband in name only.” Through the battle and eventual victory over the White Witch, Aeriel realizes that Irrylath does love her. Erin is a dark girl from Bern who Aeriel saves from a Darkangel. She is the truest friend anyone could ever have. Some of the secondary characters did not come off the page well. I was hoping to feel more for Ravenna and the White Witch. <br /><br />My biggest criticism is that Pierce uses words that do not exist in the English language. If they do exist there is not modern meaning and not in the dictionary. I understand a new vocabulary is part of the “world creator” mentality, but it irks me to not know words on a page. Pierce also uses a couple different names for the Darkangels (vampire, icari, birdman) and the White Witch (lorelei, oriencon, sorceress). It just gets confusing. Anyway, when you’re reading this prepare to concentrate. <br /><br />Overall, I think this is a good read. It will exercise your imagination and take you away if you let it. Very creative. Enjoyable. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18107949039315885503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_137289385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137289385" />
    <a title="Karissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa"><img alt="Karissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557318686p2/4057501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137289385?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karissa" href="/user/show/4057501-karissa">Karissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137289385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4278288234159472600">This is the second book in the DarkAngel trilogy. If you liked the first book you will like this book. More happens in this book and it is just as creative as the first one. You definitely need to read the first book before reading this book though.<br/><br/>In this book Aeriel is living in the palace with her Prince, Irrylath and his family; the problem is Irrylath cannot stand to be around Aeriel because he is forced to be in love with the evil water witch. When the second part of the rime/prophecy is r</span>
  <span id="freeText4278288234159472600" style="display:none">This is the second book in the DarkAngel trilogy. If you liked the first book you will like this book. More happens in this book and it is just as creative as the first one. You definitely need to read the first book before reading this book though.<br /><br />In this book Aeriel is living in the palace with her Prince, Irrylath and his family; the problem is Irrylath cannot stand to be around Aeriel because he is forced to be in love with the evil water witch. When the second part of the rime/prophecy is revealed to Ariel she is forced to go on a journey to make sure the prophecy will be fulfilled and to save Irrylath from the water witch.<br /><br />The tone of this book is similar to the first book. Aeriel very much goes with the flow. She is an interesting character in that she does not seek out action, the action comes to her. Yet, she shows admirable strength in dealing with whatever hand is dealt to her. This book is a bit more of an adventure/quest than the first one was. Aeriel does a bit less waiting around; but there is some inconsistent pacing. Again Pierce has Aeriel go through a lot of action, then times passes as Aeriel waits, then action, then more waiting.<br /><br />The storyline is very fairy-tale-like and very creative. The writing is beautiful and descriptive; at times you feel as if you are floating through the story. It was a beautiful book and a great continuation of this story. While the main story point was resolved, the major storyline remains to be resolved in the third book. I am looking forward to reading the third book as soon as I can.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4278288234159472600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_34178197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34178197" />
    <a title="A.C. Lillywhite" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1307091-a-c-lillywhite"><img alt="A.C. Lillywhite" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1219339693p2/1307091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34178197?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A.C. Lillywhite" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A.C. Lillywhite" href="/user/show/1307091-a-c-lillywhite">A.C. Lillywhite</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316067256" href="/book/show/1877307.A_Gathering_of_Gargoyles">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34178197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6229011789293151312">I sort of figured that this was probably one of those series where the first book is really the only story and after that the narrative just kind of limps along so you get the satisfaction of knowing about the rest of the main character's lives. It's not though. You can actually tell that this is the next chapter in the story. There is more to know and experience and there are still questions that you didn't even know you had about the first story. <br/><br/>More of the world opens up and we get to see ju</span>
  <span id="freeText6229011789293151312" style="display:none">I sort of figured that this was probably one of those series where the first book is really the only story and after that the narrative just kind of limps along so you get the satisfaction of knowing about the rest of the main character's lives. It's not though. You can actually tell that this is the next chapter in the story. There is more to know and experience and there are still questions that you didn't even know you had about the first story. <br /><br />More of the world opens up and we get to see just how alien this place and these people are. Like in the first one, everything has significance and a purpose and it isn't taxing yet to try and guess what that may be. The authoress gives you credit here. You're going to figure out a lot of what's going on before the characters let you know about it, but there was at least one pretty impressive surprise for me at the end.<br /><br />Probably my only major complaint would be the lack of Aerial/Irrylath. I do realise that there needed to be a certain amount of 'off camera' character development. They've got issues and this part of the story isn't really about them, but the couple of scenes they had together were quite good and pretty much a total tease. <br /><br />I'll move on to the third book tomorrow and hopefully we'll get a resolution... </span>
  <a data-text-id="6229011789293151312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_361827209" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/361827209" />
    <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers"><img alt="TheBookSmugglers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316717753p2/1223249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/361827209?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookSmugglers" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers">TheBookSmugglers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=notable-reads-of-2012">notable-reads-of-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=hidden-gems">hidden-gems</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer361827209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10979078560458896544">Originally reviewed on <a href='http://thebooksmugglers.com/2012/07/book-review-a-gathering-of-gargoyles-by-meredith-ann-pierce.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book Smugglers</a><br/><br/>After cutting out her own heart and giving it to the darkangel Irrylath, Aeriel has not only found a way to save her world from the clutches of the White Witch and her seven icari, but she has also found a way to save Irrylath's soul. After breaking the curse on her new bridegroom, Aeriel and Irrylath make their way to Isternes, the childhood home of Irrylath, before he was treacherously traded away to the White Witch by his nursemaid Dirna for life and p</span>
  <span id="freeText10979078560458896544" style="display:none">Originally reviewed on <a href="http://thebooksmugglers.com/2012/07/book-review-a-gathering-of-gargoyles-by-meredith-ann-pierce.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Smugglers</a><br /><br />After cutting out her own heart and giving it to the darkangel Irrylath, Aeriel has not only found a way to save her world from the clutches of the White Witch and her seven icari, but she has also found a way to save Irrylath's soul. After breaking the curse on her new bridegroom, Aeriel and Irrylath make their way to Isternes, the childhood home of Irrylath, before he was treacherously traded away to the White Witch by his nursemaid Dirna for life and power. Here, Irrylath finds his true mother, his brothers, and his birthright as the eldest son and heir to the land - but though he and Aeriel are welcomed with open arms by his Esternese kin, their struggles remain. <br /><br />Irrylath remains plagued by terrible dreams and withdraws from Aeriel's touch and compassion - and Aeriel learns that her husband, in name if not in truth, still is snared by the hook of the White Witch. If she is to save him - and to truly save her world from the Witch, who even now searches for a new babe to make into a darkangel - Aeriel must embark on a dangerous quest, and solve an ancient, hidden riddle.<br /><br /><em>A Gathering of Gargoyles</em> continues the story of a brave young woman named Aeriel, who has inexplicably become the one person that can stand against an evil that threatens to consumer her world. And, dear readers, I loved this book so very much. I must start this review properly by thanking the lovely Megan no h for her emphatic recommendation, because <em>A Gathering of Gargoyles</em> is truly and utterly awesome. It is in fact a better novel than <em>The Darkangel</em>; <em>The Empire Strikes Back</em> to the first novel's <em>Star Wars</em>. I know that science fiction analogy may seem at first blush NOT to make sense with this trilogy, but in actuality it has far more resonance than one might suspect - because <em>A Gathering of Gargoyles</em> makes it abundantly clear that this series is actually one rooted in science fiction. Aeriel's world, as it becomes known in <em>A Gathering of Gargoyles</em>, is actually our moon; a "daymonth" to Aeriel and her fellow creatures, is the equivalent to a lunar day, with the constant companion of the Earth, or "Oceanus" to Aeriel, shining its pale blue light upon the moon's surface. Unlike our current moon, though, Aeriel's world is a place of impossible, fantastical life - in which there are seas of dust hiding moonwhales and serpents, with deserts and forests, gargoyles and lons. <br /><br />This is the most impressive thing about this trilogy, and <em>A Gathering of Gargoyles</em> in particular - the incredible scope of <em>imagination</em>. To be sure, this is a fantasy novel with magical creatures and gifts, but the story never once feels tired or familiar because of the magic of Ms. Pierce's prose and the wildly imaginative setting. Reading <em>A Gathering of Gargoyles</em> is almost like being in a dream - things are strange and ever-shifting, but you never really feel confused or lost, because it is <em>your</em> dream, and impossible things are accepted as a matter of course. <br /><br />From a pure story perspective, the actual plot of the novel is fairly simple - Aeriel leaves Isternes to find the lost lons, so that Irrylath's brothers can ride them into battle against the White Witch - and her journey takes her to the edges of the world. In truth, the story is about Aeriel as she discovers who she is, what she is truly capable of, and how far she will go to stop the Witch and win Irrylath's heart. The riddle - actually more of a prophecy - that sparks her journey lies at the heart of the book, and I love that its meaning changes as Aeriel's self-awareness grows. <br /><br />For all that she is risking everything for Irrylath, this is truly Aeriel's story, and I loved every last second of it. I loved following Aeriel from Isternes, across the Sea-of-Dust, to singing for her sup and on the run from bandits, to the desperate land of Pirs and the terrible truth of its ruler, to eventually back in her own home of Terrain. On each leg of her far journey, Aeriel learns a new truth, gathering Irrylath's former gargoyle guards along the way. My main complaint for <em>The Darkangel</em> was Aeriel's lack of oomph, and her utter, unflinching goodness. While she is still unerringly moral and good in <em>A Gathering of Gargoyles</em>, this book shows us glimpses of her vulnerability. She falls for the tricks of a false king and a hag; she shows her frustration when all her work seems to have gone to waste. And, most touchingly, we <em>feel</em> her heart breaking as she realizes the truth of Irrylath and that he does not love her.<br /><br />This volume ends on a sweet note, with the promise of even more fantastic adventure and peril ahead - the trilogy must close with Aeriel and Irrylath's confrontation of the White Witch, and I cannot wait to find out how it all ends.<br /><br />If you haven't read this gem of a series before, I implore you to find a used copy and start. Absolutely, wholeheartedly recommended, and one of my most cherished finds of the year. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10979078560458896544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ursula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44578950-ursula"><img alt="Ursula" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537822605p2/44578950.jpg" /></a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44578950-ursula?shelf=2014-and-before">2014-and-before</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44578950-ursula?shelf=a-5-star-book">a-5-star-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44578950-ursula?shelf=g-fantasy">g-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1327786593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2552654958161662685">24 June 2019. Finished A Gathering of Gargoyles by Meredith Ann Pierce.<br/><br/>Rating - 5 stars<br/>Genre - Fantasy<br/>Sub- genre - Magic<br/>Intended Audience - Middle Grade Girls<br/>Publisher - Harcourt<br/><br/>So this is the second book in the trilogy. I don't want to give too much of an introduction to this book because I think the books are best when read in order back to back, but I will say this book has a lot of wandering in it. Wandering books can be pretty hit or miss with me, but I loved how the author pulled it off in</span>
  <span id="freeText2552654958161662685" style="display:none">24 June 2019. Finished A Gathering of Gargoyles by Meredith Ann Pierce.<br /><br />Rating - 5 stars<br />Genre - Fantasy<br />Sub- genre - Magic<br />Intended Audience - Middle Grade Girls<br />Publisher - Harcourt<br /><br />So this is the second book in the trilogy. I don't want to give too much of an introduction to this book because I think the books are best when read in order back to back, but I will say this book has a lot of wandering in it. Wandering books can be pretty hit or miss with me, but I loved how the author pulled it off in this book. There were a lot of confrontations and new characters.<br /><br />One of my favorite characters introduced was Erin. I loved her role in the story and also I loved the friendship between Aeriel and Erin. I thought the author wrote a positive female friendship where both sides care about the other and it's very different from the female friendship I've seen in other books and tv shows. There is initially fear and confusion, but trust grows between them and it feels like a real strong friendship.<br /><br />One last random topic is I like how the author lets side characters have important roles. Sometimes main characters steal the show and are written as though they're the only interesting person in the world that everyone needs to fawn over. This is especially common in YA fantasy. Pierce gives the side characters interesting backstories and allows them to be involved in moving the plot forward. At least more so than what I've seen from the average fantasy book.<br /><br />Again, I don't want to over hype this trilogy, but I love it and highly recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2552654958161662685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4460087858938521074">Another trilogy I won't bother to finish. Irrylath was far more interesting as a Darkangel than as human Irrylath. Too angsty. Thankfully he isn't around much, only in the first chapter or so and in the last one. We get to know why he can't "love" Aeriel. Not really a mystery, since the specters told Aeriel in the first book <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[that he used to be the Witch's lover, who is his adoptive mother...   <span id="freeText4460087858938521074" style="display:none">Another trilogy I won't bother to finish. Irrylath was far more interesting as a Darkangel than as human Irrylath. Too angsty. Thankfully he isn't around much, only in the first chapter or so and in the last one. We get to know why he can't "love" Aeriel. Not really a mystery, since the specters told Aeriel in the first book <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that he used to be the Witch's lover, who is his adoptive mother... Yikes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Aeriel starts a new adventure, but alas, she is not what she used to be. Or all the other characters, for that matter. Since when all the Gargoyles have names? Since when they love her so much? And everywhere she goes, she finds something useful and powerful.. things that don't look much, but she is all "oh well, I am going to take it", and turns out, they are magical stuff or super expensive stuff that helps her in her way.<br /><br />And not only she is extremely lucky to find those objects; she meets allies that help her out, or otherwise, she would have been dead by chapter 3. She isn't the sharpest girl, the poor thing accepts drinks and food from suspicious people (her uncle, Diurna) without thinking. And what does she get? Drugged, that's what. Not once, but for almost all the length of book.<br /><br />I think that her whole stay in Pirs was such a waste of time. How she did not notice a thing, from the very beginning. How she did not notice the truth about her cloak. <br /><br />2nd book in the series was a bit boring, tbh. And since I don't care anymore about Aeriel and Irrylath, til here I come.</span>

<div id="review_188218180" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/188218180" />
    <a title="Kiersten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5861997-kiersten"><img alt="Kiersten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323835889p2/5861997.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/188218180?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiersten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiersten" href="/user/show/5861997-kiersten">Kiersten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780613115650" href="/book/show/1189718.A_Gathering_of_Gargoyles">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer188218180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5726339722229802068">An excellent sequel to The Darkangel and a solid precursor to the third book of the trilogy. We learn some more history of Irrylath's enchantment, bring in a host of new characters, and awarded plenty of riveting plot twists along the way. We get a much broader picture of Aeriel's world in this installment, as she traverses half the nations and encounters different cultures and colorful people. I really enjoyed that aspect of it, and in some ways it had a "fuller" feel than the first book, as if</span>
  <span id="freeText5726339722229802068" style="display:none">An excellent sequel to The Darkangel and a solid precursor to the third book of the trilogy. We learn some more history of Irrylath's enchantment, bring in a host of new characters, and awarded plenty of riveting plot twists along the way. We get a much broader picture of Aeriel's world in this installment, as she traverses half the nations and encounters different cultures and colorful people. I really enjoyed that aspect of it, and in some ways it had a "fuller" feel than the first book, as if it's expanding on the world we only glimpsed one detailed corner of in the first book. Pierce does a good job of hinting at certain things, giving the reader enough clues to foreshadow that there's something really important about certain events or objects, but without revealing enough to give it away before the time is ripe. It very subtly adds to the suspense and holds the reader's attention without frustrating them. Aeriel is still a solid heroine, well-balanced between human and an unknown variable. I was really impressed with the way the author hints at her "strangeness" without ever really giving away if it's due to some innate power of Aeriel's or merely a result of her circumstances. I thought it was a very unique novel in many respects. Overall, I thought it was an unusually solid second book; it's written as if it's really worth your time as a novel of its own and not just to fill in the middle of a trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5726339722229802068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_27387454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27387454" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27387454?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa McShane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa McShane" href="/user/show/1329059-melissa-mcshane">Melissa McShane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780812549027" href="/book/show/1189719.A_Gathering_of_Gargoyles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1329059-melissa-mcshane?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27387454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17247267737164708184">Having rescued Irrylath and escaped to his mother's kingdom (his birth mother, not the witch who told him she was his mother), Aeriel is now stuck with a husband who won't even let her touch him and a reluctance to tell anyone the truth about where (or who) Irrylath has been for twenty-four years. When she receives the second part of Ravenna's rhyme, she sets out alone to solve it by finding and restoring the lost guardians ("lons") of the six other realms. The part that I still think is really </span>
  <span id="freeText17247267737164708184" style="display:none">Having rescued Irrylath and escaped to his mother's kingdom (his birth mother, not the witch who told him she was his mother), Aeriel is now stuck with a husband who won't even let her touch him and a reluctance to tell anyone the truth about where (or who) Irrylath has been for twenty-four years. When she receives the second part of Ravenna's rhyme, she sets out alone to solve it by finding and restoring the lost guardians ("lons") of the six other realms. The part that I still think is really cool is the revelation about where the lons have been all this time, which isn't obvious. Aeriel's heritage is way more obvious, but at least Pierce doesn't tie the story in knots trying to keep it a secret.<br /><br />On the other hand, I know as a kid I didn't appreciate the final plot complication, when Irrylath finally explains why he can't be close to Aeriel. I'm sure all I noticed was that he finally showed that he *does* care for her. The truth <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that Irrylath was the witch's lover and that he's still aroused by her in his dreams <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is far more complex and sad; it goes a long way toward making Irrylath more clearly a victim.<br /><br />As with the first book, I admire Pierce's worldbuilding, and I think this is a stronger story. I just don't love it anymore, and that makes me sad.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17247267737164708184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4463795853568275697">I liked this book better than the first, and I'm looking forward to reading the next book, but it seems like I might be the only reader who doesn't particularly like Aeriel. She just seems so clueless sometimes and some of the things she does make absolutely no sense. It seems like she can barely figure out anything for herself and everyone else is always having to give her the answers. I think the world and story are really interesting, though, and I like the side characters. I'll definitely ke</span>
  <span id="freeText4463795853568275697" style="display:none">I liked this book better than the first, and I'm looking forward to reading the next book, but it seems like I might be the only reader who doesn't particularly like Aeriel. She just seems so clueless sometimes and some of the things she does make absolutely no sense. It seems like she can barely figure out anything for herself and everyone else is always having to give her the answers. I think the world and story are really interesting, though, and I like the side characters. I'll definitely keep reading to see how it ends and I hope I grow to like Aeriel more during the next book. <br /><br />As a side note, I noticed a lot of typos in this book, just like the first one. I don't know if it's like this in all editions of the book, but it seems like really sloppy editing and it can be a bit distracting at times.</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1851966-annie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41513169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16697051200430798142">I enjoyed the second volume more than the first. The plot is allowed to stretch out more, while still staying interconnected, with no unecessary rambling.<br/><br/>Poor Aeriel is still in love with her prince-husband, but he cannot love her back, even though she has literally given him her heart. She really grows into her destined role of hero, though, and by the end of the book she is no longer a timid slave, but a force to be reckoned with. I like that it's not a feeling of destiny that drives her, thou</span>
  <span id="freeText16697051200430798142" style="display:none">I enjoyed the second volume more than the first. The plot is allowed to stretch out more, while still staying interconnected, with no unecessary rambling.<br /><br />Poor Aeriel is still in love with her prince-husband, but he cannot love her back, even though she has literally given him her heart. She really grows into her destined role of hero, though, and by the end of the book she is no longer a timid slave, but a force to be reckoned with. I like that it's not a feeling of destiny that drives her, though, but her feelings of love and affection and hope.<br /><br />I can't wait to get my hands on Volume III. At the end of this volume was a teaser, which was intense. It looks like Aeriel is going to be betrayed. She has to overcome the evil witch, but at what cost?</span>
  <a data-text-id="16697051200430798142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12927305520679880871">I am REALLY enjoying this series. This second book follows Aeriel's journey through new places/cultures as she attempts to complete a task set by a second riddle - I'm not crazy about the riddles, but the plot device holds the story together fairly well. I love the world Pierce develops and the different challenges Aeriel faces. She's not the smartest heroine in the history of fiction, but she's kind, and that gets her a long way (and given her upbringing as a slave, her naivety and lack of worl</span>
  <span id="freeText12927305520679880871" style="display:none">I am REALLY enjoying this series. This second book follows Aeriel's journey through new places/cultures as she attempts to complete a task set by a second riddle - I'm not crazy about the riddles, but the plot device holds the story together fairly well. I love the world Pierce develops and the different challenges Aeriel faces. She's not the smartest heroine in the history of fiction, but she's kind, and that gets her a long way (and given her upbringing as a slave, her naivety and lack of worldly common sense isn't surprising). <br /><br />While reading, I was reminded of a video game quest. She sets out on a journey, encountering different levels and picking up key items/loot along that way that becomes useful later when used in the right way. She meets new friends, makes new enemies, and the ever-present big boss looms in the distance biding time till the final battle. <br /><br />My edition has a lot of typos that could have used a better editor, but...it's not the worst thing.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2978164328" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2978164328" />
    <a title="Keeloca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60839319-keeloca"><img alt="Keeloca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556964409p2/60839319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2978164328?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keeloca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keeloca" href="/user/show/60839319-keeloca">Keeloca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2978164328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8771895972915411543">Actual score: 2,5.<br/><br/>Oh, no, she's on a quest now! I just don't like this particular aspect of fantasy - the endless, plodding travels! One of the strenghts of the first installments in this series is that it by and large takes place in one place. None of this senseless running about. :( But Aeriel remains a nice heroine: generally I go for more flawed characters, but in a time where ALL main characters are insistently flawed, it's nice to meet a truly good one, who manages not to be boring.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3636120570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3828248808526430748">I first read this in late elementary school, and I somehow completely missed the fact that it is set on a futuristic Moon! The story was almost as good as I remember it being, and Pierce has a great sing-song style that fits the just-enough-details-present type of mytho-narrative she has created. I wholly recommend this as a quick and easy read for any age group.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xgJV8lMmTLVJZaa5BLCWVPZMnr20TI7/WP9hFMGOtQOOa37Nya5OswIxZDVGyQIOtwXd8Z5GWG5vAIKIXZMm+w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('w/EJzyNxr0DDlz5uUpd963h+BcAce/v8PpZhiN0nNg2LmCLwufmtRojD/OIQ7umxOTdGjDZxLW0JaYIUQTql9Q==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13638905912385145073">Meredith Ann Pierce is a fantasy writer and librarian. Her books deal in fantasy worlds with mythic settings and yet overturn standard expectations, frequently featuring young women who first wish only to love and be loved, yet who must face hazard and danger to save their way of life, their world, and so on, usually without being respected for their efforts until the end of the story.</span>
